The Proofs for I'tikaf: Quran, Sunnah, and Reason
Proofs from Quran, Sunnah, and rational arguments for the merit of i'tikaf

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the three proofs for i'tikaf and explain why it is considered a sunnah muakkadah in the Hanafi school.

Core Idea
I'tikaf is a confirmed sunnah established by Quran, the Prophet's practice, and rational reflection on its spiritual benefits.

This lesson explores the legislative basis and excellence of i'tikaf (spiritual seclusion in the mosque). The author of Nur al-Idah cites three distinct sources: a Quranic verse that implies i'tikaf is an act of worship, the Prophet's unwavering practice, and a rational argument that highlights its elevated status. Understanding these proofs is essential to appreciating why i'tikaf holds a special place in Ramadan and in the life of a believer.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
Recognize that the act under discussion is i'tikaf, and the Hanafi ruling is that it is a sunnah muakkadah (confirmed sunnah). This is the base legal classification derived from the evidence.
2
Locate the Quranic dalil
Find the verse (2:187) and understand the wajh al-dalalah (indication): the prohibition of marital relations while in i'tikaf proves that i'tikaf is a recognized act of worship, because only a valid act would be accompanied by such a prohibition.
The Quranic proof has qat'i thubut but zanni dalala.
3
Examine the Sunnah proof
Identify the hadith narrated by Abu Hurairah and 'A'ishah that the Prophet consistently performed i'tikaf during the last ten days of Ramadan from his arrival in Medina until his death. The commentary of al-Zuhri reinforces that the Prophet never abandoned it.
The Sunnah provides a definitive practice (fi'l) as evidence.
4
Reflect on the rational argument
Understand the rational (ma'qul) evidence: i'tikaf involves waiting for prayer (which is like continuous prayer), detachment from worldly affairs, and surrendering to the Lord. This makes it one of the noblest acts when done with sincerity.
Rational arguments are supplementary but highlight the merit.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
والاعتكاف مشروع بالكتاب) لمـا تـلونـا مـن قوله تعالى: وَلَا تُبَاشِرُوهُنَّ وَأَنتُمْ عَكِفُونَ فِي الْمَسَاجِدِ [البقرة: 187]، فالإضافة إلى المساجد المختصة بالقرب، وترك الوطء المباح لأجله دليل على أنه قربة، والسنَّةِ) لما روى أبو هريرة وعائشة أن النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم: كَانَ يَعْتَكِفُ فِي العَشْرِ الأَوَاخِرِ مِنْ رَمَضَان مُنْدُ قَدِمَ المَدِينَةِ إِلَى أنْ تَوَفَّاهُ الله تَعَالَى، وقال الزهري : عجباً من الناس كيف تركوا الاعتكاف، ورسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم كان يفعل الشيء ويتركه، ومـا ترك الاعتكاف حتى قبض. (و) أشار إلى ثبوته بضرب من المعقول، فقال: وهـو مـنْ أَشْرَفِ الأعمال إذا كان عن إخلاص الله تعالى؛ لأنه منتظر للصلاة وهـو كـالمصلي، وهي حالة قـرب وانقطاع ) ومحاسنها لا تحصى. (ومن محاسنِهِ أنّ فيه: تفريغ القلب من أمور الدنيا) بشغله بالإقبال على العبادة متجرداً لها، وتسليم النفس إلى المولى بتفويض أمرها إلى عزيز جنابــه، والاعتماد على كرمه ( وملازمة عبادتِهِ، والتقرب إليه ليقرب من رحمته، كما أشار إليه في حديث ( مـن تقرب... » ) ملازمة القرار في بيتِهِ)، واللائق بصاحب المنزل إكرام نزيله، تفضلاً ورحمة وإحساناً ومنة، والتحصن بحصنه فلا يصل إليه عدوه بكيده وقهره؛ لقوة سلطان الله تعالى وقـهـره، وعـزيـز تأييده ونصره، ترى الرعايا يحبسون أنفسهم على باب سلطانهم وهو فرد منهم، ويجهدون في خدمته والقيام أذلة بين يديه لقضاء مآربهم، فيعطف عليهم بإحسانه ويحميهم من عدوهم بقوة سلطانه، وقــد نبه على حصول المراد وأزال حجاب الوهم وأزال الغطاء، وأظهر الحق وأماط . عنه الغطاء بما أشار إليه بقوله، (وقال) العارف بالله تعالى (عَطَاء) بن أبي رباح التابعي، تلميذ ابن عباس أحــد مشايخ الإمام الأعظم أبو حنيفة ( رحمه الله ما رأيت أفقه من حماد، ولا أجمع للعلوم من عطاء . أبي رباح، أكثر رواية الإمام أبي حنيفة عن عطاء، سمع ابن عباس وابن عمر . وأبا هريرة وأبا . وجابر وعائشة ، توفي سنة خمس عشرة ومائة، وهو ابن ثمانين سنة، كذا في « أعلام الأخيار » قال رحمه الله تعالى ونفعنا ببركته ومدده: (مَثَلُ المُعتكف مَثَلُ رَجُلٍ يَخْتَلِفُ) أي: يتردد ويقف
I'tikaf is legislated by the Book (Quran) as we recited from His statement: 'And do not have relations with them while you are in seclusion in the mosques' (2:187). So the addition to the mosques specially for nearness, and leaving permissible intercourse for its sake is evidence that it is a act of worship. And by the Sunnah, as narrated by Abu Hurairah and 'A'ishah that the Prophet ﷺ used to observe i'tikaf during the last ten days of Ramadan from the time he came to Medina until Allah took him. And al-Zuhri said: 'I am amazed at how people have abandoned i'tikaf, while the Messenger of Allah ﷺ would do some things and leave others, but he never left i'tikaf until he died.' And he pointed to its confirmation by rational argument, saying: It is among the noblest of deeds if it is done with sincerity to Allah, because he is waiting for prayer and is like one in prayer, and it is a state of closeness and detachment. Its merits are countless. Among its merits are: emptying the heart from worldly matters, surrendering the soul to the Lord, adhering to His worship, being close to Him, being in the house of one's Master, and fortifying oneself in His fortress. And 'Ata' ibn Abi Rabah said: 'The example of the one in i'tikaf is like a man who frequents...'
Source pages p. 680

Commentary
This passage establishes the legitimacy and excellence of i'tikaf from three sources: Quran, Sunnah, and rational reflection. The Quranic verse (2:187) is cited, where Allah prohibits marital relations during seclusion in mosques. The fact that He specifically mentions mosques and prohibits permissible acts indicates that i'tikaf is a form of worship (qurbah). The Sunnah proof is the consistent practice of the Prophet ﷺ who observed i'tikaf in the last ten days of Ramadan every year from his arrival in Medina until his death, as reported by Abu Hurairah and 'A'ishah. The commentary of al-Zuhri emphasizes that the Prophet never abandoned it. Then the author provides rational arguments: i'tikaf involves waiting for prayer, which is like continuous prayer; it involves detachment from worldly concerns; it is a state of closeness to Allah. The saying of 'Ata' ibn Abi Rabah likens the mu'takif to a person who constantly stands at the door of a king, implying that he is in a state of seeking and devotion.

Key Terms
مشروع (mashrū’): Legislated; established by Islamic law.
قربة (qurbah): An act of worship that brings one closer to Allah.

Key Terms from Source Passage

B) Surah al-Baqarah 2:187

Key Takeaway
I'tikaf is a confirmed sunnah (sunnah muakkadah) established by the Quran, the consistent practice of the Prophet ﷺ, and rational reflection on its spiritual benefits.

Virtue and Proof of I'tikaf as Sunnah
Expounds the virtue of i'tikaf and its evidence from Quran and Sunnah

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on i'tikaf and identify the Quranic and Prophetic evidence that establishes it as sunnah muakkadah.

Core Idea
I'tikaf is sunnah muakkadah because the Prophet never abandoned it in the last ten days of Ramadan.

I'tikaf is one of the most virtuous acts of worship, especially in the last ten days of Ramadan. This lesson examines the textual and rational evidence that establishes its recommended status in the Hanafi school. You will learn how the Quranic verse on seclusion in mosques and the Prophet's consistent practice prove that i'tikaf is sunnah muakkadah.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling on i'tikaf
The passage begins by stating i'tikaf is from the most noble deeds, and later asserts it is sunnah. In Hanafi fiqh, this refers to sunnah muakkadah.
Sunnah muakkadah is a recommended act that the Prophet consistently performed.
2
Examine the Quranic evidence
The author cites verse 2:187, which prohibits marital relations during i'tikaf in mosques. This implies i'tikaf is a recognized act of worship.
The verse does not command i'tikaf, but its mention indicates its legitimacy.
3
Examine the Prophetic practice
The hadith of Aisha and Abu Huraira states the Prophet performed i'tikaf every year in the last ten days of Ramadan from his arrival in Medina to his death.
Continuous practice (fi'l) is evidence for sunnah in Hanafi usul.
4
Consider the rational and spiritual proofs
The mu'takif is like one waiting for prayer, and the analogy with a servant standing at a king's door emphasizes the virtue of i'tikaf.
These proofs reinforce the merit but are secondary to textual evidence.
5
Note the cross-madhhab difference
While Hanafi and Shafi'i consider it sunnah muakkadah, Malik considers it mustahabb. The practical difference is the degree of emphasis.
The difference is valid and based on varying methodologies.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
والسنَّةِ. وهو منْ أَشْرَفِ الأعمال إذا كان عن إخلاص، ومن محاسنِهِ أن فيه تفريغ القلب من أمور الدنيا، وتسليم النفس إلى المولى وملازمة عبادتِهِ في بيتِهِ، والتحصن بحصنِهِ، وقال عَطَاءٌ رَحِمَهُ اللَّهُ: مَثَلُ المعتكف مَثَلُ رَجُلٍ يَخْتَلِفُ وَلَا تُبَاشِرُوهُنَّ وَأَنتُمْ عَكِفُونَ فِي الْمَسَاجِدِ [البقرة: ۱۸۷]، فالإضافة إلى المساجد المختصة بالقرب، وترك الوطء المباح لأجله دليل على أنه قربة، والسُّنَّةِ) لما روى أبو هريرة وعائشة أن النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم: كَانَ يَعْتَكِفُ فِي العَشْرِ الأَوَاخِرِ مِنْ رَمَضَان مُنْدُ قَدِمَ المَدِينَةِ إِلَى أنْ تَوَفَّاهُ الله تَعَالَى ، وقال الزهري : عجباً من الناس كيف تركوا الاعتكاف، ورسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم كان يفعل الشيء ويتركه، ومـا ترك الاعتكاف حتى قبض. (ومن محاسنِهِ أنّ فيه: تفريغ القلب من أمور الدنيا) بشغله بالإقبال على العبادة متجرداً لها، وتسليم النفس إلى المولى بتفويض أمرها إلى عزيز جنابــه، والاعتماد على كرمه ( وملازمة عبادتِهِ، والتقرب إليه ليقرب من رحمته، كما أشار إليه في حديث ( مـن تقرب... » ) ملازمة القرار في بيتِهِ)، واللائق بصاحب المنزل إكرام نزيله، تفضلاً ورحمة وإحساناً ومنة، والتحصن بحصنه فلا يصل إليه عدوه بكيده وقهره؛ لقوة سلطان الله تعالى وقـهـره، وعـزيـز تأييده ونصره، ترى الرعايا يحبسون أنفسهم على باب سلطانهم وهو فرد منهم، ويجهدون في خدمته والقيام أذلة بين يديه لقضاء مآربهم، فيعطف عليهم بإحسانه ويحميهم من عدوهم بقوة سلطانه، وقــد نبه على حصول المراد وأزال حجاب الوهم وأزال الغطاء، وأظهر الحق وأماط عنه الغطاء بما أشار إليه بقوله، (وقال) العارف بالله تعالى (عَطَاء) بن أبي رباح التابعي، تلميذ ابن عباس أحــد مشايخ الإمام الأعظم أبو حنيفة ( رحمه الله ما رأيت أفقه من حماد، ولا أجمع للعلوم من عطاء . أبي رباح، أكثر رواية الإمام أبي حنيفة عن عطاء، سمع ابن عباس وابن عمر . وأبا هريرة وأبا . وجابر وعائشة ، توفي سنة خمس عشرة ومائة، وهو ابن ثمانين سنة، كذا في « أعلام الأخيار » قال رحمه الله تعالى ونفعنا ببركته ومدده: (مَثَلُ المُعتكف مَثَلُ رَجُلٍ يَخْتَلِفُ) أي: يتردد ويقف على باب عظيم الحاجة، فالمعتكف يقولُ: لا أَبْرَحُ حَتَّى يَغْفِرَ لِي.
And it is from the most noble of deeds if it is with sincerity. Among its virtues: emptying the heart from worldly matters, surrendering the soul to the Lord, constant worship in His house, and fortifying oneself in His fortress. 'Ata' (may Allah have mercy on him) said: The example of the one in i'tikaf is like a man who goes back and forth ... and do not have relations with them while you are secluded in the mosques [2:187]. So the addition to the mosques is specific to closeness, and leaving permissible intercourse for its sake is evidence that it is an act of worship. And it is Sunnah due to what Abu Huraira and 'Aisha narrated that the Prophet (peace be upon him) used to perform i'tikaf in the last ten days of Ramadan from the time he arrived in Medina until Allah took his soul. Az-Zuhri said: Amazing are the people who abandoned i'tikaf while the Messenger of Allah did it and continued it until he passed away. And he pointed to its establishment by a rational proof, saying: It is from the most noble of deeds if it is with sincerity to Allah because he is waiting for prayer and is like one praying, and it is a state of closeness and detachment. Among its virtues: emptying the heart from worldly matters, ... and fortification in His fortress... and he said: the one who is known to Allah ('Ata' ibn Abi Rabah)... he said: The example of the mu'takif is like a man who goes back and forth and stands at the door of a great need, so the mu'takif says: I will not leave until He forgives me.
Source pages p. 680

Commentary
This passage is a commentary on the ruling that i'tikaf is sunnah. The author begins by affirming that i'tikaf is from the most noble acts when done sincerely. He lists its virtues: emptying the heart from dunya, surrendering to Allah, constant worship, and seeking protection in Allah's fortress. Then he provides the primary evidence: the Quranic verse (2:187) which prohibits marital relations during i'tikaf in mosques, indicating that it is an act of worship. Additionally, the Sunnah is established by the hadith of Aisha and Abu Huraira that the Prophet performed i'tikaf every year in the last ten days of Ramadan from his arrival in Medina until his death. Az-Zuhri's statement rebukes those who abandoned it while the Prophet never did. The author then adds a rational proof: i'tikaf is noble because the mu'takif is waiting for prayer and thus considered in a state of prayer. Further virtues are explained, including analogy with subjects standing at a king's door. Finally, the passage quotes 'Ata' ibn Abi Rabah, a tabi'i and teacher of Imam Abu Hanifa, who compares the mu'takif to a man standing at a king's door insisting for his need, saying 'I will not leave until he forgives me.' This illustrates the spiritual state of the mu'takif.

Key Terms
الاعتكاف (al-i'tikaf): Seclusion in a mosque with the intention of drawing closer to Allah, especially during the last ten days of Ramadan.
السنة (al-sunnah): A recommended act that is consistently practiced by the Prophet; not obligatory but encouraged.

Key Terms from Source Passage

B) The command to perform i'tikaf in the last ten days.
C) The story of Maryam's i'tikaf.
D) The verse on fasting.

Key Takeaway
I'tikaf in the last ten days of Ramadan is sunnah muakkadah, established by the Prophet's continuous practice and the Quranic indication of its virtue.

Sadaqat al-Fitr: Obligation, Conditions, and Amount
Defines obligation, conditions, amount, and rules of Sadaqat al-Fitr

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the obligation of Sadaqat al-Fitr, identify its conditions, calculate the required amount, and apply the rules for dependents.

Core Idea
Sadaqat al-Fitr is wajib on every free Muslim with surplus nisab at dawn of Eid—no year required.

This chapter explains the obligation of Sadaqat al-Fitr, a charity given at the end of Ramadan. The Hanafi school holds it as wajib, not fard, and its conditions differ from Zakat al-Mal. Understanding the nisab, the timing, the recipients, and the measure is essential for every Muslim. In this lesson, we will dissect the passage from Nur al-Idah with the commentary of Imdad al-Fattah.

Guided Path
1
Identify the obligated person and conditions
Start by listing the conditions for obligation: free, Muslim, legally responsible, owns nisab or its value at dawn of Eid, free from debt and basic needs, not for trade.
The nisab here is the same as Zakat but without the conditions of growth and year passage.
2
Determine the nisab and its distinction from Zakat
The nisab for Sadaqat al-Fitr is the same amount as Zakat nisab, but it does not require the wealth to be growth-oriented or owned for a full year. The text mentions three types of nisab; this one is for Sadaqat al-Fitr, sacrifice, and supporting relatives.
3
Recognise the dependents for whom one must pay
The obligation extends to oneself, young children (whether poor or rich), and certain slaves. It does not apply to the father except under specific conditions, nor to adult sons, wife, or mukatab. The grandfather is a point of ikhtilaf.
For rich children, the father pays from their wealth.
4
Learn the specified amounts and the ruling on paying value
The amount is half a sa' of wheat or its flour/sawiq, or a full sa' of dates, raisins, or barley. One sa' equals eight Iraqi ratls. Paying the cash equivalent is permissible and considered better if it meets the need.
The Iraqi ratl is 130 dirhams, so the sa' is 1040 dirhams in volume.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
باب صدقة الفطر
باب صدقة الفطر: تجب على حر مسلم، مكلف مالك لنصاب أو قيمته وإن لم يحل عليه الحول، عند طلوع فجر يوم الفطر، ولم يكن للتجارة، فارغ عن الدين وحاجته الأصلية وحوائج عياله. والمعتبر فيها الكفاية لا التقدير، وهي مسكنه، وأثاثه، وثيابه، وفرسه، وسلاحه وعبيده للخدمة، فيخرجها عن نفسه وأولاده الصغار الفقراء، وإن كانوا أغنياء يخرجها من مالهم. ولا تجب على الجد في ظاهر الرواية. واختير أن الجد كالأب عند فقده أو فقره، وعن مماليكه للخدمة، ومُدَبَّرِهِ وأم ولده ولو كفاراً، لا عن مكاتبه ولا ولده الكبير، وزوجته، وقن مشترك، وأبق إلا بعد عوده، وكذا المغصوب والمأسور، وهي: نصف صاع من بر أو دقيقه، أو سويقه، أو صاع تمر، أو زبيب، أو شعير، وهو ثمانية أرطال بالعراقي. ويجوز دفع القيمة، وهي أفضل عند وجدان ما يحتاجه لأنها أسهل.
(۱) أمر بها في السنة التي فرض فيها رمضان قبل الزكاة، وكان يخطب قبل الفطر بيومين يأمر بإخراجها، ولا تسقط بهلاك المال بعد الوجوب، بخلاف الزكاة، ط. وسبب شرعيتها ما رواه ابن عباس رضي الله عنه قال: «فرض رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم زكاة الفطر طهرة للصائم من اللغو والرفث، وطعمة للمساكين، من أداها قبل الصلاة فهي زكاة مقبولة، ومن أداها بعد الصلاة فهي صدقة من الصدقات»، أخرجه أبو داود في الزكاة، باب: زكاة الفطر (١٦٠٩). (۲) وإنما وجبت، لقوله صلى الله عليه وسلم في خطبته : « أدوا عن كل حر وعبد صغير أو كبير نصف صاع من بر، أو صاعاً من شعير، أو صاعاً من تمر » ، أخرجه أبو داود في الزكاة، باب من روى نصف صاع من قمح (١٦٢٢).
(۳) اعلم أن النصب ثلاثة : نصاب يشترط فيه النماء وتتعلق به الزكاة وسائر الأحكام المتعلقة بالمال النامي. ونصاب تجب به أحكام أربعة حرمة الصدقة، ووجوب الأضحية، وصدقة الفطر، ونفقة الأقارب، ولا يشترط فيه النمو بالتجارة، ولا حولان الحول ونصاب تثبت به حرمة السؤال، وهو ما إذا كان عنده قوت يومه عند بعض. وقال بعضهم: هو أن يملك خمسين درهماً. ط. (٤) لأن الولاية والمؤن لا ينعدمان بالتدبير والاستيلاد، وإنما تختل بهما المالية من حيث إنهما لا يباعان. فتح باب العناية (٥٥٠/١). (۵) قوله: لا عن مكاتبه، لعدم الولاية، ولا تجب على المكاتب، لأن ما في يده لمولاه. قوله: ولا ولده الكبير، أي: الفقير، وإن كان في عياله لانعدام الولاية قوله وزوجته، لعدم الولاية الكاملة عليها. قوله: وقن مشترك وابق إلا بعد عوده لقصور الولاية والمؤنة في حق كل واحد منهما قوله وكذا المغصوب والمأسور، فلا تجب على سيدهما إلا بعد عودهما فتجب لما مضى. ط.
(٦) الرطل العراقي مائة وثلاثون درهماً، فالصاع ما يسع ألفاً وأربعين درهماً. وقول أبي يوسف: الصاع ما يسع خمسة أرطال وثلثاً مراده بالرطل رطل المدينة وهو ثلاثون أستاراً، ورطل العراق عشرون أستاراً، فيكون المجموع على القولين مائة وستين أستاراً. والأستار: ستة دراهم ونصف. ط.
Chapter on Sadaqat al-Fitr. It is obligatory upon a free Muslim, legally responsible, owner of a nisab or its value even if the year has not passed, at the break of dawn of the day of Fitr, and it is not for trade, free from debt and his basic needs and the needs of his dependents. What is considered is sufficiency, not estimation; these are his dwelling, furniture, clothes, horse, weapon, and slaves for service. He pays it for himself and his young poor children; if they are rich, he pays from their wealth. It is not obligatory upon the grandfather in the apparent narration. And it is chosen that the grandfather is like the father when he is absent or poor. And for his slaves for service, his mudabbar, his umm walad even if they are disbelievers; not for his mukatab, nor his adult son, his wife, a shared slave, a runaway except after his return, likewise the usurped and the captive. It is half a sa' of wheat or its flour or its sawiq, or a sa' of dates, raisins, or barley; and it is eight ratls by Iraqi. Paying value is permissible, and it is better when finding what is needed because it is easier.
Source pages p. 686

Commentary
This passage is the chapter on Sadaqat al-Fitr. It begins by stating the obligation: it is wajib upon every free Muslim who possesses a nisab of Zakat or its value, even if a year has not passed, at dawn of Eid al-Fitr. The nisab here is not the same as Zakat; it does not require growth or a year's passage. The conditions include having surplus wealth beyond basic needs and debts. The text explains who must pay: for oneself, for young children if they are poor; if children are rich, the father pays from their wealth. There is a difference of opinion regarding the grandfather: in the apparent narration it is not obligatory, but some choose that he is like the father in his absence or poverty. Payment is also for slaves serving the family, mudabbar, umm walad even if disbelievers. Not paid for mukatab, adult son, wife, shared slave, runaway slave, etc. The amount is half a sa' of wheat or its derivatives, or a whole sa' of dates, raisins, or barley. The Iraqi ratl is used—eight ratls. Paying the value (cash equivalent) is permissible and even better if it meets the recipient's need more easily.

Key Terms
صدقة الفطر (sadaqat al-fitr): The obligatory charity given at the end of Ramadan, also called Zakat al-Fitr.
نصاب (nisab): The minimum amount of wealth that triggers obligation; here it is the nisab for Zakat but without the conditions of growth and passage of year.
صاع (sa'): A measure of volume; here half a sa' of wheat or one sa' of other grains, equivalent to 8 Iraqi ratls.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Which of the following is NOT a condition for the obligation of Sadaqat al-Fitr?
A) Free and Muslim
B) Owner of nisab at dawn of Eid
C) The nisab must have been owned for one year
D) Free from debt and basic needs

Key Takeaway
Sadaqat al-Fitr is a distinct wajib charity with its own conditions, timing, and measures, and must be paid by every qualifying Muslim before Eid prayer.

beginner

Preparation and Entering the Prophet's Mosque
Instructions for preparation before visiting Madinah and entering the mosque.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to describe the recommended acts of preparation before visiting Madinah and recite the supplications for entering the city and the Prophet's mosque.

Core Idea
Visiting Madinah is an act of reverence requiring physical and spiritual preparation.

This lesson covers the recommended etiquette before entering Madinah and the Prophet's mosque. The text guides the visitor through ghusl, perfume, attire, walking, and specific supplications. These acts reflect the visitor's love and respect for the Prophet (peace be upon him) and prepare the heart for the spiritual journey.

Guided Path
1
Identify the sequence of preparations
List the recommended acts before entering Madinah: ghusl, perfume, best clothes, and walking with humility. Note their purpose: reverence for the Prophet.
2
Recite the entrance supplications
Learn the dua recited when entering Madinah (Quran 17:80) and the mosque. Understand the meaning and importance of seeking Allah's mercy and blessings on the Prophet.
3
Understand the mosque etiquettes
Upon entering, pray tahiyyat al-masjid near the pulpit, then stand at the Prophet's former standing place. The space between the grave and pulpit is a garden of Paradise.
4
Perform the gratitude prostration
After tahiyyat, pray two additional rak'ahs or prostrate in thanks (sajdat al-shukr) for reaching Madinah safely. Then make any personal supplication.

عــن أمته أشهد أنك رسول الله قد بلغت الرسالة، وأديت الأمانة، ونصحت الأمة، وأوضحت الحجة، و جاهدت في سبيل الله حق جهاده، وأقمت الدين حتى أتاك اليقين. صلى الله عليك وسلم، وعلـى أشرف مكان تشرف بحلول جسمك الكريم فيه صلاة وسلاماً دائمين من رب العالمين عــدد مـا كـان وعدد ما يكون بعلم الله، صلاةٌ لا انقضاء لأمدها، يا رسول الله نحن وفـدَكَ وزوار حرمك، تشرفنا بالحلول بين يديك، وقد جئناك من بلاد شاسعة، وأمكنة بعيدة، نقطع السهل والوعر بقصد زيارتك، لنفوز بشفاعتك، والنظر إلى مآثرك ومعاهدك، والقيام بقضاء بعض حقك، والاستشفاع بك إلى ربنا، فإن الخطايا قد قصمت ظهورنا، والأوزار قد أثقلت كواهلنا، وأنت الشافع المشفّع، الموعود بالشفاعة العظمى، والمقام المحمود والوسيلة، وقد قال الله تعالى: ﴿وَلَوْ أَنَّهُمْ إِذْ ظَلَمُوا أَنفُسَهُمْ جَاءُوكَ فَاسْتَغْفَرُوا اللهَ وَاسْتَغْفَرَ لَهُمُ الرَّسُولُ لَوَجَدُوا اللهَ تَوَّابًا رَّحِيمًا [النساء : ٦٤]، وقد جئناك ظالمين لأنفسنا، مستغفرين لذنوبنا، فاشفع لنا إلى ربك، واسأله أن يميتنـا عـلـى سُنَّتك، وأن يحشرنا في زمرتك، وأن يوردنا حوضك، وأن يسقينا بكأسك، غير خزايا ولا ندامي الشفاعة الشفاعة الشفاعة يا رسول الله، يقولها ثلاثاً ربنا اغفر لنا، ولإخواننا الذين سبقونا بالإيمان، ولا تجعل في قلوبنا غلاً للذين آمنوا، ربَّنا إنك رؤوف رحيم. وتبلغه سلام من أوصاك به فتقول: السلام عليك يا رسول الله من فلان بن فلان يتشفّع بك إلى ربك فاشفع له وللمسلمين، ثم تصلي عليه وتدعو بما شئت عند وجهه الكريم مستدبر القبلة، ثم تتحول قدر ذراع حتى تحاذي رأس الصديق أبي بكر – رضي اليقين، سل الله سبحانه لنا دوام حبك، والحشـر مــع حزبك، وقبول زيارتنا، والسلام عليك ورحمة الله وبركاته. ثم تتحول مثل ذلك حتى تحاذي رأس أمير المؤمنين عمر بن الخطاب - رضي الله تعالى . عنه - فتقول: السلام عليك يا أمير المؤمنين، السلام عليك يا مظهر الإسلام السلام عليك يا مكسر الأصنام جزاك الله عنا أفضل الجزاء لقـد نصرت الإسلام والمسلمين، وفتحت معظم البلاد بعد سيد المرسلين، وكفلت الأيتام، ووصلت الأرحام، وقوي بك الإسلام، وكنت للمسلمين إماماً مرضياً؛ وهادياً مهدياً، جمعت شملهم، وأعنت فقيرهم، وجبرت كسرهم، السَّلام عليك ورحمة الله وبركاته، ثم ترجع قدر نصف ذراع فتقول:
Al-Mustafa on the Day of Return. And he performs ghusl before entering or after before proceeding to the visit if possible, and applies perfume, and wears his best clothes, out of reverence for coming to the Prophet (peace be upon him). Then he enters Madinah Munawwarah walking if possible without necessity after placing his knees and feeling at ease with his family and belongings, humbly with tranquility and dignity, observing the majesty of the place, saying: 'In the name of Allah and on the religion of the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him): My Lord, cause me to enter a goodly entrance and cause me to exit a goodly exit, and grant me from Yourself a supporting victory' (Quran 17:80). O Allah, send blessings upon our master Muhammad and upon the family of Muhammad, and forgive my sins, and open for me the doors of Your mercy and bounty. Then he enters the noble mosque, and prays its greeting near its pulpit two rak'ahs, and stands such that the pillar of the noble pulpit is opposite his right shoulder, for that is the standing place of the Prophet (peace be upon him), and what is between his grave and his pulpit is a garden from the gardens of Paradise, as he informed, and he said: 'My pulpit is upon my Cistern.' Then he prostrates in gratitude to Allah by performing two rak'ahs besides the greeting of the mosque, gratitude for what Allah has granted him success and bestowed upon him by reaching it. Then he supplicates as he wishes. Then he rises heading towards the noble grave, and stands about four cubits away from the noble enclosure, with utmost respect, facing away from the qiblah, aligned with the head of the Prophet (peace be upon him) and his noble face, observing his blessed gaze upon him, and his hearing of his speech, and his response to his greeting, and his saying 'Amin' to his supplication. And he says: Peace be upon you, O my master, O Messenger of Allah. Peace be upon you, O Prophet of Allah. Peace be upon you, O Beloved of Allah. Peace be upon you, O Prophet of Mercy. Peace be upon you, O Intercessor of the Ummah. Peace be upon you, O Master of the Messengers. Peace be upon you, O Seal of the Prophets. Peace be upon you, O Enwrapped One. Peace be upon you, O Enshrouded One. Peace be upon you and upon your pure roots and the purified people of your household, from whom Allah has removed impurity and purified them thoroughly. May Allah reward you on our behalf with the best that He has rewarded a prophet for his people and a messenger for his nation. I bear witness that you are the Messenger of Allah. You conveyed the message, fulfilled the trust, advised the ummah, clarified the proof, struggled in the path of Allah as is His due, and established the religion until the certainty came to you. May Allah bless you and grant you peace, and upon the most honored place honored by the settlement of your noble body in it, blessings and peace perpetually from the Lord of the worlds, to the number of what has been and what will be in Allah's knowledge, a blessing without end. O Messenger of Allah, we are your delegation and visitors of your sanctuary. We are honored to be in your presence. We have come to you from distant lands and faraway places, traversing plains and rugged terrain with the intention of visiting you, to gain your intercession, to look upon your relics and your sites, to fulfill some of your right, and to seek intercession through you to our Lord. For sins have broken our backs, and burdens have weighed down our shoulders, and you are the intercessor whose intercession is accepted, promised with the greatest intercession, the praiseworthy station, and the means. And Allah Almighty said: 'If they, when they wronged themselves, had come to you and asked forgiveness of Allah and the Messenger had asked forgiveness for them, they would have found Allah Accepting of repentance and Merciful' (Quran 4:64). And we have come to you wronging ourselves, seeking forgiveness for our sins. So intercede for us with your Lord, and ask Him to let us die upon your Sunnah, and to resurrect us in your company, and to bring us to your Cistern, and to give us to drink from your cup, not disgraced nor regretful. Intercession, intercession, intercession, O Messenger of Allah. He says it three times: Our Lord, forgive us and our brothers who preceded us in faith, and put not in our hearts any malice against those who have believed. Our Lord, indeed You are Kind and Merciful. And he conveys the greeting of whomever has instructed him to do so: Peace be upon you, O Messenger of Allah, from so-and-so son of so-and-so. He seeks intercession through you to your Lord, so intercede for him and for the Muslims. Then he sends blessings upon him and supplicates as he wishes at his noble face, facing away from the qiblah. Then he moves about a cubit until he is parallel to the head of As-Siddiq Abu Bakr (may Allah be pleased with him) and says: Peace be upon you, O Caliph of the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him). Peace be upon you, O Companion of the Messenger of Allah, his intimate in the cave, his companion in journeys, his confidant in secrets. May Allah reward you on our behalf with the best that He has rewarded an imam for the nation of his Prophet. For you succeeded him in the best manner, followed his way and methodology in the best path, fought the people of apostasy and innovation, consolidated Islam, strengthened its pillars, and you were the best imam, maintained family ties, and you continued standing for the truth, supporting the religion and its people until the certainty came to you. Ask Allah for us to have constant love for you, to be resurrected with your party, and for acceptance of our visit. Peace be upon you and the mercy of Allah and His blessings. Then he moves similarly until parallel to the head of Amir al-Mu'minin Umar ibn al-Khattab (may Allah be pleased with him) and says: Peace be upon you, O Amir al-Mu'minin. Peace be upon you, O manifestor of Islam. Peace be upon you, O breaker of idols. May Allah reward you on our behalf with the best reward. You supported Islam and the Muslims, conquered most of the lands after the Master of the Messengers, sponsored the orphans, maintained family ties, Islam was strengthened by you, and you were for the Muslims a pleasing imam, a guided guide, you united them, helped their poor, mended their brokenness. Peace be upon you and the mercy of Allah and His blessings. Then he goes back half a cubit and says: ...
Source pages p. 705

Commentary
This passage from the Hanafi fiqh commentary describes the recommended etiquette (adab) for a person visiting Medina and the Prophet's mosque, specifically focusing on the visit to the Prophet's grave. The text outlines a sequence of actions: ghusl, applying perfume, wearing best clothes, entering Medina walking, supplications, entering the mosque, praying tahiyyat al-masjid, standing at the pulpit, prostrating in gratitude, then proceeding to the grave. At the grave, the visitor stands four cubits away, facing away from the qiblah, and recites a lengthy greeting praising the Prophet and testifying to his message. The supplication includes seeking intercession (shafa'ah) and forgiveness. After greeting the Prophet, the visitor moves to greet Abu Bakr al-Siddiq and then Umar ibn al-Khattab with specific salutations. The passage emphasizes reverence, humility, and the belief that the Prophet hears and responds to greetings. The footnotes (not included here) cite hadith about the space between the grave and pulpit being a garden of Paradise and the pulpit being upon the Prophet's Cistern. Hanafi fiqh considers visiting the Prophet's grave as mustahabb (recommended) based on the practice of the Companions and the hadith encouraging visits. This text serves as a practical guide for the ziyarah, blending devotional acts with prescribed supplications.

Key Terms
زيارة (ziyarah): The act of visiting the Prophet's mosque and grave in Medina.
السلام (as-salam): The greeting of peace; in this context, it is a form of respect and supplication addressed to the Prophet and his companions.
تحية المسجد (tahiyyat al-masjid): The two-rak'ah prayer performed upon entering the mosque as a greeting to the mosque.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what does the visitor recite upon entering Madinah?
A) Surah Al-Fatihah
B) The supplication from Quran 17:80
C) The Shahadah
D) Dua for entering the mosque

Key Takeaway
Preparation for visiting Madinah involves physical purification, supplication, and following the Prophet's example with humility and reverence.

Visiting the Prophet's Grave and the Two Caliphs
Detailed instructions for visiting the Prophet's grave and greeting the two caliphs.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to describe the proper etiquette for greeting the Prophet at his grave and recite the prescribed salutations to Abu Bakr and Umar.

Core Idea
Greeting the Prophet at his grave is an act of reverence and seeking his intercession.

This lesson details the recommended way to approach the Prophet's grave, stand respectfully, and recite the lengthy greeting. It then guides the visitor to greet Abu Bakr and Umar with specific words. The text emphasizes the belief that the Prophet hears the greeting and responds, and that seeking his intercession is permissible.

Guided Path
1
Approach the grave with adab
Stand about four cubits away from the enclosure, facing away from the qiblah, aligned with the Prophet's head. Observe utmost respect, believing he sees and hears you.
2
Recite the greeting and testimony
Say 'As-salamu 'alayka' with various honorific titles, then bear witness that he conveyed the message. Ask for intercession and recite Quran 4:64.
3
Convey greetings from others
If someone has sent greetings, convey them: 'As-salamu 'alayka ya Rasul Allah min [name].' Then pray for them.
4
Greet Abu Bakr al-Siddiq
Move one cubit to be parallel to his head. Recite the prescribed greeting, acknowledging his virtues and caliphate.
5
Greet Umar ibn al-Khattab
Move similarly to be parallel to his head. Recite the greeting, praising his role in Islam and conquests.
Then return half a cubit and continue with further supplications.

عليك ياسيدي يـا ! رسول الله، السلام عليك يا نبي الله السلام عليك يا حبيب الله السلام عليك يا نبي الرحمة، السلام عليك يا شفيع الأمة، السلام عليك يا سيد المرسلين، السلام عليك يا خاتم النبيين، الســلام عـلـيـك يــا مُزَّمِّلُ، السلام عليك يا مُدَّثِّرُ، السلام عليك، وعلى أصولك الطيبين، وأهل بيتك الطاهرين، الذين أذهب الله عنهم الرجس وطهرهم تطهيراً، جزاك الله عنا أفضل ما جزى نبياً عن قومه، ورسولاً عــن أمته أشهد أنك رسول الله قد بلغت الرسالة، وأديت الأمانة، ونصحت الأمة، وأوضحت الحجة، و جاهدت في سبيل الله حق جهاده، وأقمت الدين حتى أتاك اليقين. صلى الله عليك وسلم، وعلـى أشرف مكان تشرف بحلول جسمك الكريم فيه صلاة وسلاماً دائمين من رب العالمين عــدد مـا كـان وعدد ما يكون بعلم الله، صلاةٌ لا انقضاء لأمدها، يا رسول الله نحن وفـدَكَ وزوار حرمك، تشرفنا بالحلول بين يديك، وقد جئناك من بلاد شاسعة، وأمكنة بعيدة، نقطع السهل والوعر بقصد زيارتك، لنفوز بشفاعتك، والنظر إلى مآثرك ومعاهدك، والقيام بقضاء بعض حقك، والاستشفاع بك إلى ربنا، فإن الخطايا قد قصمت ظهورنا، والأوزار قد أثقلت كواهلنا، وأنت الشافع المشفّع، الموعود بالشفاعة العظمى، والمقام المحمود والوسيلة، وقد قال الله تعالى: ﴿وَلَوْ أَنَّهُمْ إِذْ ظَلَمُوا أَنفُسَهُمْ جَاءُوكَ فَاسْتَغْفَرُوا اللهَ وَاسْتَغْفَرَ لَهُمُ الرَّسُولُ لَوَجَدُوا اللهَ تَوَّابًا رَّحِيمًا [النساء : ٦٤]، وقد جئناك ظالمين لأنفسنا، مستغفرين لذنوبنا، فاشفع لنا إلى ربك، واسأله أن يميتنـا عـلـى سُنَّتك، وأن يحشرنا في زمرتك، وأن يوردنا حوضك، وأن يسقينا بكأسك، غير خزايا ولا ندامي الشفاعة الشفاعة الشفاعة يا رسول الله، يقولها ثلاثاً ربنا اغفر لنا، ولإخواننا الذين سبقونا بالإيمان، ولا تجعل في قلوبنا غلاً للذين آمنوا، ربَّنا إنك رؤوف رحيم. وتبلغه سلام من أوصاك به فتقول: السلام عليك يا رسول الله من فلان بن فلان يتشفّع بك إلى ربك فاشفع له وللمسلمين، ثم تصلي عليه وتدعو بما شئت عند وجهه الكريم مستدبر القبلة، ثم تتحول قدر ذراع حتى تحاذي رأس الصديق أبي بكر – رضي الله تعالى عنه - وتقول: السلام عليك يا خليفة رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم ، السلام عليــك يـا صاحب رسول الله، وأنيسه في الغار، ورفيقه في الأسفار، وأمينه في الأسرار، جزاك الله عنا أفضل ما جزى إماماً عن أمة نبيه، فلقد خلفته بأحسن خلف، وسلكت طريقه ومنهاجـه خـيـر مسلك، وقاتلت أهل الردة والبدع، ومهدت الإسلام، وشيدت أركانه، فكنت خير إمام، ووصلت الأرحام، ولم تزل قائماً بالحق ناصراً للدين ولأهله حتى أتاك اليقين، سل الله سبحانه لنا دوام حبك، والحشـر مــع حزبك، وقبول زيارتنا، والسلام عليك ورحمة الله وبركاته. ثم تتحول مثل ذلك حتى تحاذي رأس أمير المؤمنين عمر بن الخطاب - رضي الله تعالى . عنه - فتقول: السلام عليك يا أمير المؤمنين، السلام عليك يا مظهر الإسلام السلام عليك يا مكسر الأصنام جزاك الله عنا أفضل الجزاء لقـد نصرت الإسلام والمسلمين، وفتحت معظم البلاد بعد سيد المرسلين، وكفلت الأيتام، ووصلت الأرحام، وقوي بك الإسلام، وكنت للمسلمين إماماً مرضياً؛ وهادياً مهدياً، جمعت شملهم، وأعنت فقيرهم، وجبرت كسرهم، السَّلام عليك ورحمة الله وبركاته، ثم ترجع قدر نصف ذراع فتقول:
Al-Mustafa on the Day of Return. And he performs ghusl before entering or after before proceeding to the visit if possible, and applies perfume, and wears his best clothes, out of reverence for coming to the Prophet (peace be upon him). Then he enters Madinah Munawwarah walking if possible without necessity after placing his knees and feeling at ease with his family and belongings, humbly with tranquility and dignity, observing the majesty of the place, saying: 'In the name of Allah and on the religion of the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him): My Lord, cause me to enter a goodly entrance and cause me to exit a goodly exit, and grant me from Yourself a supporting victory' (Quran 17:80). O Allah, send blessings upon our master Muhammad and upon the family of Muhammad, and forgive my sins, and open for me the doors of Your mercy and bounty. Then he enters the noble mosque, and prays its greeting near its pulpit two rak'ahs, and stands such that the pillar of the noble pulpit is opposite his right shoulder, for that is the standing place of the Prophet (peace be upon him), and what is between his grave and his pulpit is a garden from the gardens of Paradise, as he informed, and he said: 'My pulpit is upon my Cistern.' Then he prostrates in gratitude to Allah by performing two rak'ahs besides the greeting of the mosque, gratitude for what Allah has granted him success and bestowed upon him by reaching it. Then he supplicates as he wishes. Then he rises heading towards the noble grave, and stands about four cubits away from the noble enclosure, with utmost respect, facing away from the qiblah, aligned with the head of the Prophet (peace be upon him) and his noble face, observing his blessed gaze upon him, and his hearing of his speech, and his response to his greeting, and his saying 'Amin' to his supplication. And he says: Peace be upon you, O my master, O Messenger of Allah. Peace be upon you, O Prophet of Allah. Peace be upon you, O Beloved of Allah. Peace be upon you, O Prophet of Mercy. Peace be upon you, O Intercessor of the Ummah. Peace be upon you, O Master of the Messengers. Peace be upon you, O Seal of the Prophets. Peace be upon you, O Enwrapped One. Peace be upon you, O Enshrouded One. Peace be upon you and upon your pure roots and the purified people of your household, from whom Allah has removed impurity and purified them thoroughly. May Allah reward you on our behalf with the best that He has rewarded a prophet for his people and a messenger for his nation. I bear witness that you are the Messenger of Allah. You conveyed the message, fulfilled the trust, advised the ummah, clarified the proof, struggled in the path of Allah as is His due, and established the religion until the certainty came to you. May Allah bless you and grant you peace, and upon the most honored place honored by the settlement of your noble body in it, blessings and peace perpetually from the Lord of the worlds, to the number of what has been and what will be in Allah's knowledge, a blessing without end. O Messenger of Allah, we are your delegation and visitors of your sanctuary. We are honored to be in your presence. We have come to you from distant lands and faraway places, traversing plains and rugged terrain with the intention of visiting you, to gain your intercession, to look upon your relics and your sites, to fulfill some of your right, and to seek intercession through you to our Lord. For sins have broken our backs, and burdens have weighed down our shoulders, and you are the intercessor whose intercession is accepted, promised with the greatest intercession, the praiseworthy station, and the means. And Allah Almighty said: 'If they, when they wronged themselves, had come to you and asked forgiveness of Allah and the Messenger had asked forgiveness for them, they would have found Allah Accepting of repentance and Merciful' (Quran 4:64). And we have come to you wronging ourselves, seeking forgiveness for our sins. So intercede for us with your Lord, and ask Him to let us die upon your Sunnah, and to resurrect us in your company, and to bring us to your Cistern, and to give us to drink from your cup, not disgraced nor regretful. Intercession, intercession, intercession, O Messenger of Allah. He says it three times: Our Lord, forgive us and our brothers who preceded us in faith, and put not in our hearts any malice against those who have believed. Our Lord, indeed You are Kind and Merciful. And he conveys the greeting of whomever has instructed him to do so: Peace be upon you, O Messenger of Allah, from so-and-so son of so-and-so. He seeks intercession through you to your Lord, so intercede for him and for the Muslims. Then he sends blessings upon him and supplicates as he wishes at his noble face, facing away from the qiblah. Then he moves about a cubit until he is parallel to the head of As-Siddiq Abu Bakr (may Allah be pleased with him) and says: Peace be upon you, O Caliph of the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him). Peace be upon you, O Companion of the Messenger of Allah, his intimate in the cave, his companion in journeys, his confidant in secrets. May Allah reward you on our behalf with the best that He has rewarded an imam for the nation of his Prophet. For you succeeded him in the best manner, followed his way and methodology in the best path, fought the people of apostasy and innovation, consolidated Islam, strengthened its pillars, and you were the best imam, maintained family ties, and you continued standing for the truth, supporting the religion and its people until the certainty came to you. Ask Allah for us to have constant love for you, to be resurrected with your party, and for acceptance of our visit. Peace be upon you and the mercy of Allah and His blessings. Then he moves similarly until parallel to the head of Amir al-Mu'minin Umar ibn al-Khattab (may Allah be pleased with him) and says: Peace be upon you, O Amir al-Mu'minin. Peace be upon you, O manifestor of Islam. Peace be upon you, O breaker of idols. May Allah reward you on our behalf with the best reward. You supported Islam and the Muslims, conquered most of the lands after the Master of the Messengers, sponsored the orphans, maintained family ties, Islam was strengthened by you, and you were for the Muslims a pleasing imam, a guided guide, you united them, helped their poor, mended their brokenness. Peace be upon you and the mercy of Allah and His blessings. Then he goes back half a cubit and says: ...
Source pages p. 705

Commentary
This passage from the Hanafi fiqh commentary describes the recommended etiquette (adab) for a person visiting Medina and the Prophet's mosque, specifically focusing on the visit to the Prophet's grave. The text outlines a sequence of actions: ghusl, applying perfume, wearing best clothes, entering Medina walking, supplications, entering the mosque, praying tahiyyat al-masjid, standing at the pulpit, prostrating in gratitude, then proceeding to the grave. At the grave, the visitor stands four cubits away, facing away from the qiblah, and recites a lengthy greeting praising the Prophet and testifying to his message. The supplication includes seeking intercession (shafa'ah) and forgiveness. After greeting the Prophet, the visitor moves to greet Abu Bakr al-Siddiq and then Umar ibn al-Khattab with specific salutations. The passage emphasizes reverence, humility, and the belief that the Prophet hears and responds to greetings. The footnotes (not included here) cite hadith about the space between the grave and pulpit being a garden of Paradise and the pulpit being upon the Prophet's Cistern. Hanafi fiqh considers visiting the Prophet's grave as mustahabb (recommended) based on the practice of the Companions and the hadith encouraging visits. This text serves as a practical guide for the ziyarah, blending devotional acts with prescribed supplications.

Key Terms
زيارة (ziyarah): The act of visiting the Prophet's mosque and grave in Medina.
السلام (as-salam): The greeting of peace; in this context, it is a form of respect and supplication addressed to the Prophet and his companions.
شفاعة (shafa'ah): Intercession; the visitor asks the Prophet to intercede on their behalf before Allah.
الصديق (as-Siddiq): Title of Abu Bakr, meaning 'the truthful' or 'the verifier'.
أمير المؤمنين (Amir al-Mu'minin): Title meaning 'Commander of the Faithful', used for Umar ibn al-Khattab and later caliphs.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
After greeting the Prophet, how far does the visitor move to stand parallel to the head of Abu Bakr?
A) Half a cubit
B) One cubit
C) Four cubits
D) Two cubits

Key Takeaway
Visiting the Prophet's grave requires respectful distance, specific greetings, and belief that he hears and responds, followed by salutations to his two noble companions.

Salah — Prayer
intermediate
8 min
Greeting the Prophet and His Companions
Describes recommended acts for visitors to Medina

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to recite the recommended supplications when greeting the Prophet, Abu Bakr, and Umar at their graves and explain the Hanafi basis for seeking intercession.

Core Idea
Greeting the Prophet with prescribed supplications is a recommended act of devotion.

When visiting the Prophet's Mosque in Medina, the Hanafi school recommends a sequence of acts to honour the Prophet and seek blessings. The first step is to stand before the grave and offer specific greetings and supplications. This lesson covers the recommended salutations and prayers, including the verse from Surah al-Nisa that supports seeking intercession through the Prophet.

Guided Path
1
Identify the location and direction
The visitor stands before the grave of the Prophet, facing the qibla, and addresses the Prophet and his two companions (Abu Bakr and Umar) with a formal greeting.
The two companions are buried alongside the Prophet.
2
Recite the standard greeting
The visitor says: 'Peace be upon you both, O two companions of the Messenger of Allah...' and continues with a praise of their roles.
This greeting acknowledges their status and the visitor's intention to seek intercession.
3
Stand at the head and recite the intercession verse
The visitor moves to the head of the Prophet's grave and recites verse 4:64, which mentions seeking forgiveness through the Prophet.
This verse is taken as evidence that seeking intercession through the Prophet even after his death is permissible.
4
Make personal supplications
After the verse, the visitor makes personal supplications for himself, his parents, and all Muslims.
The text provides sample supplications but allows the visitor to add any good dua.
5
Understand the ruling level
These acts are recommended (mustahabb), not obligatory (wajib). The visitor is not sinning if they omit them, but performing them brings reward.
This distinguishes the Hanafi position from other schools that may consider similar acts impermissible.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
السلام عليكما يا ضجيعي رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم ورفيقيه، ووزيريه، ومشيريه، والمعاونين له على القيام بالدين، والقائمين بعده بمصالح المسلمين، جزاكما الله أحسن الجزاء، جئناكما نتوسل بكما إلى رسول الله ليشفع لنا، ويسأل الله ربنا أن يتقبل سعينا، ويحيينا على ملته، ويميتنا عليها، ويحشرنا في زمرته، ثم يدعو لنفسه ولوالديه، ولمن أوصاه بالدعاء ولجميع المسلمين. ثم يقف عند رأس النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم كالأول ويقول اللهم إنك قلت وقولك الحق وَلَوْ أَنَّهُمْ إِذْ ظَلَمُوا أَنفُسَهُمْ جَاءُوكَ فَاسْتَغْفَرُوا اللَّهَ وَاسْتَغْفَرَ لَهُمُ الرَّسُولُ لَوَجَدُوا اللهَ تَوَّابًا رَحِيمًا [النساء : ٦٤] وقد جئناك سامعين قولك طائعين أمرك، مستشفعين بنبيك إليك. اللهم ربنا اغفر لنا، ولآبائنا وأمهاتنا، وإخواننا الذين سبقونا بالإيمان، ولا تجعل في قلوبنا غلاً للذين آمنوا، ربَّنا إِنَّك رؤوف رحيم ﴿رَبَّنَا ابْنَا فِي الدُّنْيَا حَسَنَةً وَفِي الْآخِرَةِ حَسَنَةً وَقِنَا عَذَابَ النَّارِ ﴾ [البقرة: ٢٠١] سُبْحَانَ رَبِّكَ رَبِّ الْعِزَّةِ عَمَّا يَصِفُونَ وَسَلَامُ عَلَى الْمُرْسَلِينَ وَالْحَمْدُ لِلَّهِ رَبِّ الْعَالَمِينَ ﴾ [الصافات ] ويزيد ما شاء، ويدعو بما حضره، ويوفق له بفضل الله
ثم يأتي أسطوانة أبي لبابة التي ربط بها نفسه حتى تاب الله عليه وهي بين القبر والمنبر، ويصلي ما شاء نفلاً، ويتوب إلى الله، ويدعو بما شاء، ويأتي الروضة فيصلي ما شاء، ويدعو بما أحب، ويكثر من التسبيح، والتهليل، والثناء، والاستغفار. ثم يأتي المنبر فيضع يده على الرمانة التي كانت به تبركاً بأثر رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم ، ومكان يده الشريفة إذا خطب، لينال بركته ، ويصلي عليه، ويسأل الله ما شاء، ثم يأتي الأسطوانة الحنانة، وهي التي فيها بقية الجذع، الذي حنَّ إلى النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم ، حين تركه وخطب على المنبر، حتى نزل فاحتضنه فسكن، ويتبرك بما بقي من الآثار النبوية... والأماكن الشريفة)، ويجتهد في إحياء الليالي مدة إقامته، واغتنام مشاهدة الحضرة النبوية، وزيارته في عموم الأوقات. ويستحب أن يخرج إلى البقيع، فيأتي المشاهد والمزارات خصوصاً قبر سيد الشهداء حمزة رضي الله عنه، ثم إلى البقيع الآخر، فيزور العباس، والحسن بن علي، وبقية آل الرسول رضي الله عنهم. ويزور أمير المؤمنين عثمان بن عفان رضي الله عنه، وإبراهيم ابن النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم وأزواج النبي ، وعمته صفية، والصحابة والتابعين رضي الله عنهم، ويزور شهداء أحد، وإن تيسر يوم الخميس فهو أحسن، ويقول : سَلَامُ عَلَيْكُم بِمَا صَبَرْتُمْ فَنِعْمَ عُقْبَى الدَّارِ ﴾ [الهند: ٤٢] ويقرأ آية الكرسي والإخلاص إحدى عشرة مرة، وسورة لي إن تيسر، ويهدي ثواب ذلك لجميع الشهداء ومن بجوارهم من المؤمنين. ويستحب أن يأتي مسجد قباء يوم السبت أو غيره، ويصلي فيه، ويقول بعد دعائه بما أحب يا صريخ المستصرخين يا غياث المستغيثين يا مفرج كرب المكروبين، يا مجيب
(١) أي: رفيقيه في مدفنه.
(٢) عن ابن عباس رضي الله عنه قال: غزا رسول الله [ غزوة تبوك ] فتخلف عنه عشرة أنفس منهم أبو لبابة، ثم أن أبا لبابة ورجلين معه تفكروا وندموا وأيقنوا بالهلاك، وقالوا نحن في الظلال والطمأنينة مع النساء ورسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم والمؤمنون معه في الجهاد، والله لنوثقن أنفسنا بالسواري فلا نطلقها حتى يكون رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم هو الذي يطلقها، فربط أبو لبابة نفسه بسارية وقال: والله لا أحل نفسي منها ولا أذوق طعاماً ولا شراباً حتى يتوب الله علي أو أموت فمكث سبعة أيام لا يذوق طعاماً ولا شراباً حتى ذهب سمعه فما يكاد يسمع وكاد أن يذهب بصره، وكانت ابنته تحله إذا حضرت الصلاة أو أراد أن يذهب لحاجة ، وإذا فرغ أعادته إلى الرباط حتى خر مغشاً عليه، ثم تاب الله عليه فقيل له: قد تاب الله عليك يا أبا لبابة، فقال: والله لا أحـــل نفسي حتى يكون رسول وهو الذي يحلني، فجاء رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم فحله بيده تفسير الطبري (٢٢١/٩) بتصرف.
- ٧٠٦ -

والأماكن الشريفة)، ويجتهد في إحياء الليالي مدة إقامته، واغتنام مشاهدة الحضرة النبوية، وزيارته في عموم الأوقات. ويستحب أن يخرج إلى البقيع، فيأتي المشاهد والمزارات خصوصاً قبر سيد الشهداء حمزة رضي الله عنه، ثم إلى البقيع الآخر، فيزور العباس، والحسن بن علي، وبقية آل الرسول رضي الله عنهم. ويزور أمير المؤمنين عثمان بن عفان رضي الله عنه، وإبراهيم ابن النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم وأزواج النبي ، وعمته صفية، والصحابة والتابعين رضي الله عنهم، ويزور شهداء أحد، وإن تيسر يوم الخميس فهو أحسن، ويقول : سَلَامُ عَلَيْكُم بِمَا صَبَرْتُمْ فَنِعْمَ عُقْبَى الدَّارِ ﴾ [الهند: ٤٢] ويقرأ آية الكرسي والإخلاص إحدى عشرة مرة، وسورة لي إن تيسر، ويهدي ثواب ذلك لجميع الشهداء ومن بجوارهم من المؤمنين. ويستحب أن يأتي مسجد قباء يوم السبت أو غيره، ويصلي فيه، ويقول بعـــد دعائه بما أحب يا صريخ المستصرخين يا غياث المستغيثين يا مفرج كرب المكروبين، يا مجيب
(١) كان أصحاب النبي يتبركون بأجزاء النبي الله وآثاره وثيابه وشرابه وطعامه، وذلك لإيمانهم بأن أجزاءه الشريفة وآثاره الكريمة هي . مليئة بالخيرات والبركات، وفي ذلك ما روى مسلم عن أنس، قال: «رأيت رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم والحلاق يحلقه، وأطاف به أصحابه، فما يريدون أن تقع شعرة إلا في يد رجل»، وعنه أيضاً قال: «كان رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم إذا صلى الغداة جاء خدم المدينة بانيتهم فيها الماء، فما يؤتى بإناء، إلا غمس يده فيها، فربما جاؤه في الغداة الباردة فيغمس يده فيها قال الإمام النووي - رحمه الله -: وهذا بيان ما كانت الصحابة عليـــه من التبرك بآثاره ، وتبركهم بإدخال يده الكريمة في الآنية، وتبركهم بشعره الكريم، وإكرامهم إياه أن يقع شيء منه، أخرجه مسلم في الفضائل، باب: قرب النبي عليه الصلاة والسلام من الناس وتبركـهـم بـه (٥٩٩٦ - ٥٩٩٧). وعن أنس أيضاً قال: ( كان النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم يدخل بيت أم سليم فينام على فراشها، وليست فيه، قال: فجاء ذات يوم فنام على فراشها، فأتيت فقيل لها هذا النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم نام في بيتك، على فراشك، قال: فجاءت وقــد عــرق، واستنقع عرقه على قطعة أديم على الفراش، ففتحت عتيدتها فجعلت تنشف ذلك العرق فتعصره في قواريرها، ففزع النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم فقال: «ما تصنعين يا أم سليم؟» فقالت: يا رسول الله نرجو بركته لصبياننا، قال: أصبتِ» أخرجه مسلم في الفضائل، باب: طيب عرق النبيل و التبرك به (٦٠١٠) ، وروى الإمام أحمـد عــن أنس رضي ا الله عنه قال: حدثتني أمي أن رسول الله دخل عليها، وفي بيتها قربة معلقة، قالت: فشــرب مــن القربة قائماً فعمدت إلى فم القربة فقطعتها أخرجه أحمد في مسنده (٣٧٦/٦) ، والمعنى أن أم سليم رضي
الله عنها قطعت فم القربة الذي هو موضع شربه واحتفظت به في بيتها للتبرك بأثر النبي . (٢) لما روى ابن عمر رضي الله عنهما قال: «كان النبي يأتي مسجد قباء كل سبت سبت ماشياً وراكبـاً، وفي روايــة فيصلي فيه» أخرجه البخاري في التطوع، باب من أتى مسجد قباء كل سبت (١١٩٣-١١٩٤).
-۷۰۷ -
Peace be upon you both, O two companions of the Messenger of Allah, may Allah bless him and grant him peace, and his two friends, his two ministers, his two advisors, and his helpers in establishing the religion, and those who after him took charge of the affairs of the Muslims. May Allah reward you both with the best reward. We have come to you, seeking intercession through you to the Messenger of Allah that he may intercede for us, and ask Allah, our Lord, to accept our endeavor, to keep us alive on his religion, to cause us to die upon it, and to gather us in his company. Then he supplicates for himself, his parents, those who asked him to pray for them, and all Muslims. Then he stands at the head of the Prophet, may Allah bless him and grant him peace, like the first and says: O Allah, You said, and Your word is truth: 'And if, when they wronged themselves, they had come to you, [O Muhammad], and asked forgiveness of Allah and the Messenger had asked forgiveness for them, they would have found Allah Accepting of repentance and Merciful' [Al-Nisa: 64]. And we have come to You, hearing Your word and obeying Your command, seeking intercession through Your Prophet to You. O Allah, our Lord, forgive us, our fathers, our mothers, and our brothers who preceded us in faith, and place not in our hearts any resentment toward those who have believed. Our Lord, indeed You are Kind and Merciful. 'Our Lord, give us in this world [that which is] good and in the Hereafter [that which is] good and protect us from the punishment of the Fire' [Al-Baqarah: 201]. 'Exalted is your Lord, the Lord of might, above what they describe. And peace upon the messengers. And praise to Allah, Lord of the worlds' [Al-Saffat]. And he adds whatever he wishes, and supplicates with what is present to his mind, and he will be granted success by Allah's favor. Then he comes to the pillar of Abu Lubaba, to which he tied himself until Allah accepted his repentance, and it is between the grave and the minbar. He prays there whatever nawafil he wishes, repents to Allah, and supplicates whatever he wishes. Then he comes to the Rawdah, prays whatever he wishes, supplicates whatever he loves, and frequently glorifies Allah, declares His oneness, praises Him, and seeks His forgiveness. Then he comes to the minbar, places his hand on the pomegranate that was on it, as a blessing from the trace of the Messenger of Allah, may Allah bless him and grant him peace, and the place of his noble hand when he gave the sermon, to attain its blessing. He sends blessings upon him, and asks Allah whatever he wishes. Then he comes to the yearning pillar (al-ustuwanah al-hannanah), which contains the remnant of the trunk that yearned for the Prophet, may Allah bless him and grant him peace, when he left it and began to give the sermon from the minbar, until he descended and embraced it, and it became calm. He seeks blessings from what remains of the prophetic relics... and the noble places. He strives to revive the nights during his stay, to avail himself of witnessing the prophetic presence, and to visit him at all times. It is recommended that he go out to al-Baqi', and visit the shrines and tombs, especially the grave of the master of martyrs Hamza, may Allah be pleased with him, then to the other Baqi' to visit al-Abbas, al-Hasan ibn Ali, and the rest of the family of the Messenger, may Allah be pleased with them. He visits the Commander of the Faithful Uthman ibn Affan, may Allah be pleased with him, Ibrahim the son of the Prophet, may Allah bless him and grant him peace, the wives of the Prophet, his aunt Safiyyah, the Companions and the Followers, may Allah be pleased with them, and he visits the martyrs of Uhud. If Thursday is convenient, it is better. He says: 'Peace be upon you for what you patiently endured. And excellent is the final home' [Al-Ra'd: 24]. He recites Ayat al-Kursi and Al-Ikhlas eleven times, and if possible, Surat Ya-Sin, and dedicates the reward of that to all the martyrs and the believers around them. It is recommended that he come to Masjid Quba on Saturday or another day, pray there, and say after his supplication whatever he likes: O Responder to those who cry out, O Helper of those who seek help, O Reliever of the distress of the distressed, O Answerer.
Source pages p. 707

Commentary
This passage describes the recommended acts (mustahabbat) for a visitor to the Prophet's Mosque in Medina. The author outlines a sequence of actions: first, greeting the Prophet and his two companions (Abu Bakr and Umar) with specific supplications, then standing at the head of the Prophet's grave and reciting verses and prayers, including the verse from Surah al-Nisa encouraging seeking forgiveness through the Prophet. The visitor then visits the pillar of Abu Lubaba (which commemorates his repentance), prays nawafil there, then goes to the Rawdah (the area between the minbar and the Prophet's grave) to pray and supplicate. Next, he touches the minbar's pomegranate ornament as a blessing, and visits the 'yearning pillar' which contains a remnant of the palm trunk that yearned for the Prophet. The visitor is encouraged to spend nights in worship, visit the Baqi' cemetery to greet the martyrs and companions, especially Hamza, and to recite Quran and dedicate its reward to them. Visiting Masjid Quba on Saturday is also recommended. The passage includes footnotes providing evidence for the practices of tabarruk (seeking blessings from the Prophet's relics) and the story of Abu Lubaba.

Key Terms
التبرك (al-tabarruk): Seeking blessings by touching or using objects associated with the Prophet.
التوسل (al-tawassul): Seeking intercession or means of approach through the Prophet.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, what is the ruling on reciting the supplication that includes verse 4:64 at the Prophet's grave?
A) Wajib (obligatory)
B) Sunnah Mustahabbah (recommended)
C) Makruh (disliked)
D) Haram (impermissible)

Key Takeaway
Greeting the Prophet with the prescribed supplication, including verse 4:64, is a recommended act that honours the visit and aligns with Hanafi fiqh.

Salah — Prayer
intermediate
8 min
Visiting the Pillar of Abu Lubaba and the Rawdah
Describes recommended acts for visitors to Medina

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the significance of the Pillar of Abu Lubaba and the Rawdah, and state the recommended actions (prayer, repentance, supplication) at these locations.

Core Idea
The Pillar of Abu Lubaba is a place of repentance; the Rawdah is a garden of Paradise where prayer is meritorious.

After greeting the Prophet, the visitor proceeds to two significant spots in the Mosque: the Pillar of Abu Lubaba, where a Companion tied himself in repentance until his repentance was accepted, and the Rawdah, which is a blessed area between the minbar and the grave. The Hanafi school recommends performing voluntary prayers and supplications at these places to seek blessings and forgiveness.

Guided Path
1
Locate the Pillar of Abu Lubaba
The pillar is situated between the grave and the minbar. It marks the spot where Abu Lubaba tied himself until Allah accepted his repentance.
The story of Abu Lubaba is a lesson in sincere repentance.
2
Perform nafl prayers and repentance
At this pillar, the visitor prays whatever voluntary (nafl) prayers he wishes, repents to Allah, and makes personal supplications.
The text does not specify a fixed number of rak'ahs; any nafl is permissible.
3
Move to the Rawdah
The visitor then proceeds to the Rawdah, the area between the grave and the minbar, which the Prophet described as a garden from the gardens of Paradise.
This area is highly blessed; prayer here is considered particularly rewardable.
4
Pray and supplicate in the Rawdah
The visitor prays as much as he wishes in the Rawdah, with frequent glorification (tasbih), declaration of Allah's oneness (tahlil), praise (thana'), and seeking forgiveness (istighfar).
The emphasis is on abundance of dhikr.
5
Understand the ruling level
All these acts are mustahabb (recommended). The visitor is not required to perform them; they are opportunities for extra reward.
The pillars themselves are not objects of worship but historical markers.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
السلام عليكما يا ضجيعي رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم ورفيقيه، ووزيريه، ومشيريه، والمعاونين له على القيام بالدين، والقائمين بعده بمصالح المسلمين، جزاكما الله أحسن الجزاء، جئناكما نتوسل بكما إلى رسول الله ليشفع لنا، ويسأل الله ربنا أن يتقبل سعينا، ويحيينا على ملته، ويميتنا عليها، ويحشرنا في زمرته، ثم يدعو لنفسه ولوالديه، ولمن أوصاه بالدعاء ولجميع المسلمين. ثم يقف عند رأس النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم كالأول ويقول اللهم إنك قلت وقولك الحق وَلَوْ أَنَّهُمْ إِذْ ظَلَمُوا أَنفُسَهُمْ جَاءُوكَ فَاسْتَغْفَرُوا اللَّهَ وَاسْتَغْفَرَ لَهُمُ الرَّسُولُ لَوَجَدُوا اللهَ تَوَّابًا رَحِيمًا [النساء : ٦٤] وقد جئناك سامعين قولك طائعين أمرك، مستشفعين بنبيك إليك. اللهم ربنا اغفر لنا، ولآبائنا وأمهاتنا، وإخواننا الذين سبقونا بالإيمان، ولا تجعل في قلوبنا غلاً للذين آمنوا، ربَّنا إِنَّك رؤوف رحيم ﴿رَبَّنَا ابْنَا فِي الدُّنْيَا حَسَنَةً وَفِي الْآخِرَةِ حَسَنَةً وَقِنَا عَذَابَ النَّارِ ﴾ [البقرة: ٢٠١] سُبْحَانَ رَبِّكَ رَبِّ الْعِزَّةِ عَمَّا يَصِفُونَ وَسَلَامُ عَلَى الْمُرْسَلِينَ وَالْحَمْدُ لِلَّهِ رَبِّ الْعَالَمِينَ ﴾ [الصافات ] ويزيد ما شاء، ويدعو بما حضره، ويوفق له بفضل الله
ثم يأتي أسطوانة أبي لبابة التي ربط بها نفسه حتى تاب الله عليه وهي بين القبر والمنبر، ويصلي ما شاء نفلاً، ويتوب إلى الله، ويدعو بما شاء، ويأتي الروضة فيصلي ما شاء، ويدعو بما أحب، ويكثر من التسبيح، والتهليل، والثناء، والاستغفار. ثم يأتي المنبر فيضع يده على الرمانة التي كانت به تبركاً بأثر رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم ، ومكان يده الشريفة إذا خطب، لينال بركته ، ويصلي عليه، ويسأل الله ما شاء، ثم يأتي الأسطوانة الحنانة، وهي التي فيها بقية الجذع، الذي حنَّ إلى النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم ، حين تركه وخطب على المنبر، حتى نزل فاحتضنه فسكن، ويتبرك بما بقي من الآثار النبوية... والأماكن الشريفة)، ويجتهد في إحياء الليالي مدة إقامته، واغتنام مشاهدة الحضرة النبوية، وزيارته في عموم الأوقات. ويستحب أن يخرج إلى البقيع، فيأتي المشاهد والمزارات خصوصاً قبر سيد الشهداء حمزة رضي الله عنه، ثم إلى البقيع الآخر، فيزور العباس، والحسن بن علي، وبقية آل الرسول رضي الله عنهم. ويزور أمير المؤمنين عثمان بن عفان رضي الله عنه، وإبراهيم ابن النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم وأزواج النبي ، وعمته صفية، والصحابة والتابعين رضي الله عنهم، ويزور شهداء أحد، وإن تيسر يوم الخميس فهو أحسن، ويقول : سَلَامُ عَلَيْكُم بِمَا صَبَرْتُمْ فَنِعْمَ عُقْبَى الدَّارِ ﴾ [الهند: ٤٢] ويقرأ آية الكرسي والإخلاص إحدى عشرة مرة، وسورة لي إن تيسر، ويهدي ثواب ذلك لجميع الشهداء ومن بجوارهم من المؤمنين. ويستحب أن يأتي مسجد قباء يوم السبت أو غيره، ويصلي فيه، ويقول بعد دعائه بما أحب يا صريخ المستصرخين يا غياث المستغيثين يا مفرج كرب المكروبين، يا مجيب
(١) أي: رفيقيه في مدفنه.
(٢) عن ابن عباس رضي الله عنه قال: غزا رسول الله [ غزوة تبوك ] فتخلف عنه عشرة أنفس منهم أبو لبابة، ثم أن أبا لبابة ورجلين معه تفكروا وندموا وأيقنوا بالهلاك، وقالوا نحن في الظلال والطمأنينة مع النساء ورسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم والمؤمنون معه في الجهاد، والله لنوثقن أنفسنا بالسواري فلا نطلقها حتى يكون رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم هو الذي يطلقها، فربط أبو لبابة نفسه بسارية وقال: والله لا أحل نفسي منها ولا أذوق طعاماً ولا شراباً حتى يتوب الله علي أو أموت فمكث سبعة أيام لا يذوق طعاماً ولا شراباً حتى ذهب سمعه فما يكاد يسمع وكاد أن يذهب بصره، وكانت ابنته تحله إذا حضرت الصلاة أو أراد أن يذهب لحاجة ، وإذا فرغ أعادته إلى الرباط حتى خر مغشاً عليه، ثم تاب الله عليه فقيل له: قد تاب الله عليك يا أبا لبابة، فقال: والله لا أحـــل نفسي حتى يكون رسول وهو الذي يحلني، فجاء رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم فحله بيده تفسير الطبري (٢٢١/٩) بتصرف.
- ٧٠٦ -

والأماكن الشريفة)، ويجتهد في إحياء الليالي مدة إقامته، واغتنام مشاهدة الحضرة النبوية، وزيارته في عموم الأوقات. ويستحب أن يخرج إلى البقيع، فيأتي المشاهد والمزارات خصوصاً قبر سيد الشهداء حمزة رضي الله عنه، ثم إلى البقيع الآخر، فيزور العباس، والحسن بن علي، وبقية آل الرسول رضي الله عنهم. ويزور أمير المؤمنين عثمان بن عفان رضي الله عنه، وإبراهيم ابن النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم وأزواج النبي ، وعمته صفية، والصحابة والتابعين رضي الله عنهم، ويزور شهداء أحد، وإن تيسر يوم الخميس فهو أحسن، ويقول : سَلَامُ عَلَيْكُم بِمَا صَبَرْتُمْ فَنِعْمَ عُقْبَى الدَّارِ ﴾ [الهند: ٤٢] ويقرأ آية الكرسي والإخلاص إحدى عشرة مرة، وسورة لي إن تيسر، ويهدي ثواب ذلك لجميع الشهداء ومن بجوارهم من المؤمنين. ويستحب أن يأتي مسجد قباء يوم السبت أو غيره، ويصلي فيه، ويقول بعـــد دعائه بما أحب يا صريخ المستصرخين يا غياث المستغيثين يا مفرج كرب المكروبين، يا مجيب
(١) كان أصحاب النبي يتبركون بأجزاء النبي الله وآثاره وثيابه وشرابه وطعامه، وذلك لإيمانهم بأن أجزاءه الشريفة وآثاره الكريمة هي . مليئة بالخيرات والبركات، وفي ذلك ما روى مسلم عن أنس، قال: «رأيت رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم والحلاق يحلقه، وأطاف به أصحابه، فما يريدون أن تقع شعرة إلا في يد رجل»، وعنه أيضاً قال: «كان رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم إذا صلى الغداة جاء خدم المدينة بانيتهم فيها الماء، فما يؤتى بإناء، إلا غمس يده فيها، فربما جاؤه في الغداة الباردة فيغمس يده فيها قال الإمام النووي - رحمه الله -: وهذا بيان ما كانت الصحابة عليـــه من التبرك بآثاره ، وتبركهم بإدخال يده الكريمة في الآنية، وتبركهم بشعره الكريم، وإكرامهم إياه أن يقع شيء منه، أخرجه مسلم في الفضائل، باب: قرب النبي عليه الصلاة والسلام من الناس وتبركـهـم بـه (٥٩٩٦ - ٥٩٩٧). وعن أنس أيضاً قال: ( كان النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم يدخل بيت أم سليم فينام على فراشها، وليست فيه، قال: فجاء ذات يوم فنام على فراشها، فأتيت فقيل لها هذا النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم نام في بيتك، على فراشك، قال: فجاءت وقــد عــرق، واستنقع عرقه على قطعة أديم على الفراش، ففتحت عتيدتها فجعلت تنشف ذلك العرق فتعصره في قواريرها، ففزع النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم فقال: «ما تصنعين يا أم سليم؟» فقالت: يا رسول الله نرجو بركته لصبياننا، قال: أصبتِ» أخرجه مسلم في الفضائل، باب: طيب عرق النبيل و التبرك به (٦٠١٠) ، وروى الإمام أحمـد عــن أنس رضي ا الله عنه قال: حدثتني أمي أن رسول الله دخل عليها، وفي بيتها قربة معلقة، قالت: فشــرب مــن القربة قائماً فعمدت إلى فم القربة فقطعتها أخرجه أحمد في مسنده (٣٧٦/٦) ، والمعنى أن أم سليم رضي
الله عنها قطعت فم القربة الذي هو موضع شربه واحتفظت به في بيتها للتبرك بأثر النبي . (٢) لما روى ابن عمر رضي الله عنهما قال: «كان النبي يأتي مسجد قباء كل سبت سبت ماشياً وراكبـاً، وفي روايــة فيصلي فيه» أخرجه البخاري في التطوع، باب من أتى مسجد قباء كل سبت (١١٩٣-١١٩٤).
-۷۰۷ -
Peace be upon you both, O two companions of the Messenger of Allah, may Allah bless him and grant him peace, and his two friends, his two ministers, his two advisors, and his helpers in establishing the religion, and those who after him took charge of the affairs of the Muslims. May Allah reward you both with the best reward. We have come to you, seeking intercession through you to the Messenger of Allah that he may intercede for us, and ask Allah, our Lord, to accept our endeavor, to keep us alive on his religion, to cause us to die upon it, and to gather us in his company. Then he supplicates for himself, his parents, those who asked him to pray for them, and all Muslims. Then he stands at the head of the Prophet, may Allah bless him and grant him peace, like the first and says: O Allah, You said, and Your word is truth: 'And if, when they wronged themselves, they had come to you, [O Muhammad], and asked forgiveness of Allah and the Messenger had asked forgiveness for them, they would have found Allah Accepting of repentance and Merciful' [Al-Nisa: 64]. And we have come to You, hearing Your word and obeying Your command, seeking intercession through Your Prophet to You. O Allah, our Lord, forgive us, our fathers, our mothers, and our brothers who preceded us in faith, and place not in our hearts any resentment toward those who have believed. Our Lord, indeed You are Kind and Merciful. 'Our Lord, give us in this world [that which is] good and in the Hereafter [that which is] good and protect us from the punishment of the Fire' [Al-Baqarah: 201]. 'Exalted is your Lord, the Lord of might, above what they describe. And peace upon the messengers. And praise to Allah, Lord of the worlds' [Al-Saffat]. And he adds whatever he wishes, and supplicates with what is present to his mind, and he will be granted success by Allah's favor. Then he comes to the pillar of Abu Lubaba, to which he tied himself until Allah accepted his repentance, and it is between the grave and the minbar. He prays there whatever nawafil he wishes, repents to Allah, and supplicates whatever he wishes. Then he comes to the Rawdah, prays whatever he wishes, supplicates whatever he loves, and frequently glorifies Allah, declares His oneness, praises Him, and seeks His forgiveness. Then he comes to the minbar, places his hand on the pomegranate that was on it, as a blessing from the trace of the Messenger of Allah, may Allah bless him and grant him peace, and the place of his noble hand when he gave the sermon, to attain its blessing. He sends blessings upon him, and asks Allah whatever he wishes. Then he comes to the yearning pillar (al-ustuwanah al-hannanah), which contains the remnant of the trunk that yearned for the Prophet, may Allah bless him and grant him peace, when he left it and began to give the sermon from the minbar, until he descended and embraced it, and it became calm. He seeks blessings from what remains of the prophetic relics... and the noble places. He strives to revive the nights during his stay, to avail himself of witnessing the prophetic presence, and to visit him at all times. It is recommended that he go out to al-Baqi', and visit the shrines and tombs, especially the grave of the master of martyrs Hamza, may Allah be pleased with him, then to the other Baqi' to visit al-Abbas, al-Hasan ibn Ali, and the rest of the family of the Messenger, may Allah be pleased with them. He visits the Commander of the Faithful Uthman ibn Affan, may Allah be pleased with him, Ibrahim the son of the Prophet, may Allah bless him and grant him peace, the wives of the Prophet, his aunt Safiyyah, the Companions and the Followers, may Allah be pleased with them, and he visits the martyrs of Uhud. If Thursday is convenient, it is better. He says: 'Peace be upon you for what you patiently endured. And excellent is the final home' [Al-Ra'd: 24]. He recites Ayat al-Kursi and Al-Ikhlas eleven times, and if possible, Surat Ya-Sin, and dedicates the reward of that to all the martyrs and the believers around them. It is recommended that he come to Masjid Quba on Saturday or another day, pray there, and say after his supplication whatever he likes: O Responder to those who cry out, O Helper of those who seek help, O Reliever of the distress of the distressed, O Answerer.
Source pages p. 707

Commentary
This passage describes the recommended acts (mustahabbat) for a visitor to the Prophet's Mosque in Medina. The author outlines a sequence of actions: first, greeting the Prophet and his two companions (Abu Bakr and Umar) with specific supplications, then standing at the head of the Prophet's grave and reciting verses and prayers, including the verse from Surah al-Nisa encouraging seeking forgiveness through the Prophet. The visitor then visits the pillar of Abu Lubaba (which commemorates his repentance), prays nawafil there, then goes to the Rawdah (the area between the minbar and the Prophet's grave) to pray and supplicate. Next, he touches the minbar's pomegranate ornament as a blessing, and visits the 'yearning pillar' which contains a remnant of the palm trunk that yearned for the Prophet. The visitor is encouraged to spend nights in worship, visit the Baqi' cemetery to greet the martyrs and companions, especially Hamza, and to recite Quran and dedicate its reward to them. Visiting Masjid Quba on Saturday is also recommended. The passage includes footnotes providing evidence for the practices of tabarruk (seeking blessings from the Prophet's relics) and the story of Abu Lubaba.

Key Terms
الروضة (al-Rawdah): The area between the Prophet's grave and his minbar, considered a garden of Paradise.
أسطوانة أبي لبابة (ustuwanat Abi Lubaba): The pillar where Abu Lubaba tied himself in repentance.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the recommended action at the pillar of Abu Lubaba according to the Hanafi school?
A) Recite Surah Yasin
B) Perform nafl prayer and repent
C) Touch and kiss the pillar
D) Make a wish

Key Takeaway
The pillar of Abu Lubaba and the Rawdah are recommended places for prayer, repentance, and dhikr during a visit to the Prophet's Mosque.
